             <small>
              (Kwasio)
             </small>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            5.4%
            <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">
             Igbo
            </a>
            and others
            <sup>
             a
            </sup>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>

      <p>
       <b>
        Equatorial Guinea
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         Guinea Ecuatorial
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         Guinée équatoriale
        </span>
       </i>
       , Portuguese:
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         Guiné Equatorial
        </span>
       </i>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Equatorial Guinea
       </b>
       (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         República de Guinea Ecuatorial
        </span>
       </i>
       , French:
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         République de Guinée équatoriale
        </span>
       </i>
       , Portuguese:
       <i>
        <span lang="pt">
         República da Guiné Equatorial
        </span>
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a country located in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">
        Central Africa
       </a>
       , with an area of 28,000 square kilometres (11,000 sq mi). Formerly the colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Guinea" title="Spanish Guinea">
        Spanish Guinea
       </a>
       , its post-independence name evokes its location near both the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        Equator
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">
        Gulf of Guinea
       </a>
       . Equatorial Guinea is the only sovereign African state in which
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       is an official language. As of 2015
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the country had an estimated population of 1,222,245.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea consists of two parts, an insular and a mainland region. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islands_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islands of Equatorial Guinea">
        insular region
       </a>
       consists of the islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Bioko
       </a>
       (formerly
       <i>
        Fernando Pó
       </i>
       ) in the Gulf of Guinea and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" title="Annobón Province">
        Annobón
       </a>
       , a small volcanic island which is the only part of the country south of the
       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">
        equator
       </a>
       . Bioko Island is the northernmost part of Equatorial Guinea and is the site of the country's capital,
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">
        Malabo
       </a>
       . The island nation of
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">
        São Tomé and Príncipe
       </a>
       is located between Bioko and Annobón. The mainland region,
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">
        Río Muni
       </a>
       , is bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">
        Cameroon
       </a>
       on the north and
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       on the south and east. It is the location of
       <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">
        Bata
       </a>
       , Equatorial Guinea's largest city, and
       <a href="/wiki/Oyala" title="Oyala">
        Oyala
       </a>
       , the country's planned future capital. Rio Muni also includes several small offshore islands, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Corisco" title="Corisco">
        Corisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Grande" title="Elobey Grande">
        Elobey Grande
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Chico" title="Elobey Chico">
        Elobey Chico
       </a>
       . The country is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        African Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Francophonie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
        OPEC
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">
        CPLP
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the mid-1990s, Equatorial Guinea has become one of
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       's largest oil producers. It is the richest country per capita in Africa,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and its
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        gross domestic product
       </a>
       (GDP) adjusted for
       <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
        purchasing power parity
       </a>
       (PPP) per capita ranks 43rd in the world;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the wealth is distributed extremely unevenly and few people have benefited from the oil riches. The country ranks 135th on the UN's 2016
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
        Human Development Index
       </a>
       . The UN says that less than half of the population has access to clean drinking water and that 20% of children die before reaching the age of five.
      </p>
      <p>
       The country's authoritarian government has one of the worst human rights records in the world, consistently ranking among the "worst of the worst" in
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">
        Freedom House
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">
        annual survey of political and civil rights
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
        Reporters Without Borders
       </a>
       ranks President
       <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo" title="Teodoro Obiang Nguema Mbasogo">
        Teodoro Obiang Nguema Mbasogo
       </a>
       among its "predators" of press freedom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Human trafficking in Equatorial Guinea">
        Human trafficking
       </a>
       is a significant problem; the 2012 U.S.Trafficking in Persons Report stated that Equatorial Guinea "is a source and destination for women and children subjected to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unfree_labor" title="Unfree labor">
        forced labor
       </a>
       and FC sex trafficking." The report rates Equatorial Guinea as a government that does not fully comply with minimum standards and is not making significant efforts to do so."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

            <span class="tocnumber">
             3.3
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Administrative divisions
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">
         <a href="#Economy">
          <span class="tocnumber">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="History of Equatorial Guinea">
        History of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (August 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">
        Pygmies
       </a>
       probably once lived in the continental region that is now Equatorial Guinea, but are today found only in isolated pockets in southern Río Muni.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_people" title="Bantu people">
        Bantu
       </a>
       migrations between the 18th and 19th centuries brought coastal ethno-linguistic groups as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/Fang_people" title="Fang people">
        Fang people
       </a>
       . Elements of the latter may have generated the
       <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
        Bubi
       </a>
       , who migrated from Cameroon to Río Muni and Bioko in several waves and succeeded former
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Neolithic
       </a>
       populations. The
       <a href="/wiki/Annobonese_Creole" title="Annobonese Creole">
        Annobón
       </a>
       population, originally native to
       <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">
        Angola
       </a>
       , was introduced by the Portuguese via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_island" title="São Tomé island">
        São Tomé island
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="First_European_contact_.281472.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_European_contact_(1472)">
        First European contact (1472)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First European contact (1472)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese explorer
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_do_P%C3%B3" title="Fernão do Pó">
        Fernando Pó
       </a>
       , seeking a path to
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       , is credited as being the first European to discover the island of Bioko in 1472. He called it
       <i>
        Formosa
       </i>
       ("Beautiful"), but it quickly took on the name of its European discoverer.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernando_P%C3%B3_(island)" title="Fernando Pó (island)">
        Fernando Pó
       </a>
       and Annobón were colonized by
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       in 1474.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1778, Queen
       <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">
        Maria I of Portugal
       </a>
       and King
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">
        Charles III of Spain
       </a>
       signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_El_Pardo_(1778)" title="Treaty of El Pardo (1778)">
        Treaty of El Pardo
       </a>
       which ceded
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Bioko
       </a>
       , adjacent islets, and commercial rights to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bight_of_Bonny" title="Bight of Bonny">
        Bight of Biafra
       </a>
       between the
       <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">
        Niger
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ogoue_River" title="Ogoue River">
        Ogoue
       </a>
       rivers to
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spain
       </a>
       . Spain thereby tried to gain access to a source of slaves controlled by British merchants. Between 1778 and 1810, the territory of Equatorial Guinea was administered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_the_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Viceroyalty of the Río de la Plata">
        Viceroyalty of the Río de la Plata
       </a>
       , based in
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1827 to 1843, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       had a base on
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Bioko
       </a>
       to control the
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        slave trade
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which was moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">
        Sierra Leone
       </a>
       under an agreement with Spain in 1843. In 1844, on restoration of Spanish sovereignty, the area became known as the "Territorios Españoles del Golfo de Guinea." Spain had neglected to occupy the large area in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Biafra" title="Bight of Biafra">
        Bight of Biafra
       </a>
       to which it had right by
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">
        treaty
       </a>
       , and the French had busily expanded their occupation at the expense of the area claimed by Spain. The
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1900)" title="Treaty of Paris (1900)">
        treaty of Paris
       </a>
       in 1900 left Spain with the continental
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enclave" title="Enclave">
        enclave
       </a>
       of Rio Muni, a mere 26,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       out of the 300,000 stretching east to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">
        Ubangi river
       </a>
       which the Spaniards had initially claimed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarence-Smith_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clarence-Smith-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">
        plantations
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Fernando Pó
       </a>
       were mostly run by a black
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creole_elite" title="Creole elite">
        Creole elite
       </a>
       , later known as
       <a href="/wiki/Fernandino_peoples" title="Fernandino peoples">
        Fernandinos
       </a>
       . The British occupied the island briefly in the early 19th century, settling some 2,000 Sierra Leoneans and freed slaves there. Limited immigration from West Africa and the West Indies continued after the British left. To this were added Cubans, Filipinos and Spaniards of various colours deported for political or other crimes, as well as some assisted settlers.
      </p>
      <p>
       There was also a trickle of immigration from the neighbouring Portuguese islands, escaped slaves and prospective planters. Although a few of the
       <a href="/wiki/Fernandino_peoples" title="Fernandino peoples">
        Fernandinos
       </a>
       were Catholic and Spanish-speaking, about nine-tenths of them were Protestant and English-speaking on the eve of the First World War, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pidgin_English" title="Pidgin English">
        pidgin English
       </a>
       was the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
         lingua franca
        </a>
       </i>
       of the island. The Sierra Leoneans were particularly well placed as planters while labor recruitment on the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Windward_coast&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Windward coast (page does not exist)">
        Windward coast
       </a>
       continued, for they kept family and other connections there and could easily arrange a supply of labor.
      </p>
      <p>
       The opening years of the twentieth century saw a new generation of Spanish immigrants. Land regulations issued in 1904–1905 favoured Spaniards, and most of the later big planters arrived from Spain after that. The Liberian labor agreement of 1914
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       favoured wealthy men with ready access to the state, and the shift in labor supplies from Liberia to Rio Muni increased this advantage. In 1940, an estimated 20% of the colony's cocoa production came from African-owned land, nearly all of it was in the hands of Fernandinos.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="489" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg/220px-Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg/330px-Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg/440px-Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corisco-Saliendo_de_misa-1910.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Corisco" title="Corisco">
          Corisco
         </a>
         , 1910
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The greatest constraint to
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">
        economic development
       </a>
       was a chronic shortage of labour. Pushed into the interior of the island and decimated by alcohol addiction, venereal disease,
       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">
        smallpox
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">
        sleeping sickness
       </a>
       , the indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
        Bubi
       </a>
       population of
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Bioko
       </a>
       refused to work on
       <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">
        plantations
       </a>
       . Working their own small
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       farms gave them a considerable degree of autonomy.
      </p>
      <p>
       By the late nineteenth century, the Bubi were protected from the demands of the planters by Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Claretians" title="Claretians">
        Claretian
       </a>
       missionaries, who were very influential in the colony and eventually organised the Bubi into little mission theocracies reminiscent of the famous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reducciones" title="Reducciones">
        reductions
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       . Catholic penetration was furthered by two small insurrections in 1898 and 1910 protesting
       <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">
        conscription
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_labor" title="Forced labor">
        forced labour
       </a>
       for the plantations. The Bubi were disarmed in 1917, and left dependent on the missionaries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarence-Smith_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clarence-Smith-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1926 and 1959 Bioko and Rio Muni were united as the colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Guinea" title="Spanish Guinea">
        Spanish Guinea
       </a>
       . The economy was based on large
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cacao
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       plantations and
       <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">
        logging
       </a>
       concessions and the workforce was mostly immigrant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contract_labour" title="Contract labour">
        contract labour
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">
        Liberia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroun" title="Cameroun">
        Cameroun
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Between 1914 and 1930, an estimated 10,000 Liberians went to Fernando Po under a labour treaty that was stopped altogether in 1930.
      </p>
      <p>
       With Liberian workers were no longer available, planters of Fernando Po turned to Rio Muni. Campaigns were mounted to subdue the
       <a href="/wiki/Fang_people" title="Fang people">
        Fang people
       </a>
       in the 1920s, at the time that Liberia was beginning to cut back on recruitment. There were garrisons of the colonial guard throughout the enclave by 1926, and the whole colony was considered 'pacified' by 1929.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rio Muni had a small population, officially a little over 100,000 in the 1930s, and escape across the frontiers into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroun" title="Cameroun">
        Cameroun
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       was very easy. Also, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timber" title="Timber">
        timber
       </a>
       companies needed increasing numbers of workers, and the spread of
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       cultivation offered an alternative means of paying taxes
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . Fernando Pó thus continued to suffer from labour shortages. The French only briefly permitted recruitment in Cameroun, and the main source of labour came to be
       <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">
        Igbo
       </a>
       smuggled in canoes from
       <a href="/wiki/Calabar" title="Calabar">
        Calabar
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       . This resolution to the worker shortage allowed Fernando Pó to become one of Africa's most productive agricultural areas after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">
        Second World War
       </a>
       . I
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarence-Smith_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Clarence-Smith-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Politically, post-war colonial history has three fairly distinct phases: up to 1959, when its status was raised from 'colonial' to 'provincial', following the approach of the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese Empire
       </a>
       ; between 1960 and 1968, when Madrid attempted a partial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">
        decolonisation
       </a>
       aimed at keeping the territory as part of the Spanish system; and from 1968 on, after the territory became an independent
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       . The first phase consisted of little more than a continuation of previous policies; these closely resembled the policies of Portugal and France, notably in dividing the population into a vast majority governed as 'natives' or non-citizens, and a very small minority (together with whites) admitted to civic status as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Emancipados" title="Emancipados">
         emancipados
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">
        assimilation
       </a>
       to the metropolitan culture being the only permissible means of advancement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This 'provincial' phase saw the beginnings of
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
        nationalism
       </a>
       , but chiefly among small groups who had taken refuge from the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Caudillo" title="Caudillo">
         Caudillo
        </a>
       </i>
       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
        '
       </span>
       s paternal hand in Cameroun and Gabon. They formed two bodies: the
       <a href="/wiki/Atanasio_Ndongo_Miyone" title="Atanasio Ndongo Miyone">
        Movimiento Nacional de Liberación de la Guinea
       </a>
       (MONALIGE), and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Idea_Popular_de_la_Guinea_Ecuatorial&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Idea Popular de la Guinea Ecuatorial (page does not exist)">
        Idea Popular de la Guinea Ecuatorial
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Idea_Popular_de_la_Guinea_Ecuatorial" title="es:Idea Popular de la Guinea Ecuatorial">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       (IPGE). The pressure they could bring to bear was weak, but the general trend in West Africa was not.
      </p>
      <p>
       A decision of 9 August 1963, approved by a referendum of 15 December 1963, gave the territory a measure of autonomy and the administrative promotion of a 'moderate' group, the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Movimiento_de_Uni%C3%B3n_Nacional_de_la_Guinea_Ecuatorial&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Movimiento de Unión Nacional de la Guinea Ecuatorial (page does not exist)">
        Movimiento de Unión Nacional de la Guinea Ecuatorial
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Movimiento_de_Uni%C3%B3n_Nacional_de_la_Guinea_Ecuatorial" title="es:Movimiento de Unión Nacional de la Guinea Ecuatorial">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       (MUNGE). This proved a feeble instrument, and, with growing pressure for change from the UN, Madrid gave way to the currents of nationalism.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281968.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1968)">
        Independence (1968)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Independence (1968)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Independence was conceded on 12 October 1968 and the region became the Republic of Equatorial Guinea.
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mac%C3%ADas_Nguema" title="Francisco Macías Nguema">
        Francisco Macías Nguema
       </a>
       was elected president.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 1970,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macias_Nguema" title="Macias Nguema">
        Macias Nguema
       </a>
       created a
       <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">
        single-party state
       </a>
       and made himself
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_for_life" title="President for life">
        president for life
       </a>
       in 1972. He broke off ties with Spain and the West. In spite of his condemnation of
       <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">
        Marxism
       </a>
       , which he deemed "neo-colonialist", Equatorial Guinea maintained very special relations with socialist countries, notably
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">
        USSR
       </a>
       . He signed a preferential
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_agreement" title="Trade agreement">
        trade agreement
       </a>
       and a shipping treaty with the Soviet Union. The Soviets also made loans to Equatorial Guinea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aworawo103_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aworawo103-26">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The shipping agreement gave the Soviets permission for a pilot
       <a href="/wiki/Fishery" title="Fishery">
        fishery
       </a>
       development project and also a naval base at
       <a href="/wiki/Luba,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Luba, Equatorial Guinea">
        Luba
       </a>
       . In return the USSR was to supply fish to Equatorial Guinea. China and Cuba also gave different forms of financial, military, and technical assistance to Equatorial Guinea, which got them a measure of influence there. For the USSR, there was an advantage to be gained in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angola_Civil_War" title="Angola Civil War">
        War in Angola
       </a>
       from access to Luba base and later on to
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">
        Malabo International Airport
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aworawo103_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aworawo103-26">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1974 the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Council_of_Churches" title="World Council of Churches">
        World Council of Churches
       </a>
       affirmed that large numbers of people had been murdered since 1968 in an ongoing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reign_of_terror" title="Reign of terror">
        reign of terror
       </a>
       . A quarter of the entire population had fled abroad, they said, while 'the prisons are overflowing and to all intents and purposes form one vast concentration camp'. Out of a population of 300,000, an estimated 80,000 were killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Apart from allegedly committing
       <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
        genocide
       </a>
       against the ethnic minority
       <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
        Bubi people
       </a>
       , he ordered the deaths of thousands of suspected opponents, closed down churches and presided over the economy's collapse as skilled citizens and foreigners fled the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On Christmas 1975, Macías Nguema had 150 alleged coup plotters executed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The nephew of Macías Nguema,
       <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo" title="Teodoro Obiang Nguema Mbasogo">
        Teodoro Obiang
       </a>
       deposed Macías Nguema on 3 August 1979, in a bloody
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">
         coup d'état
        </a>
       </i>
       . Macias Nguema was tried and executed soon afterward.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1995
       <a href="/wiki/Mobil" title="Mobil">
        Mobil
       </a>
       , an American oil company, discovered oil in Equatorial Guinea. The country subsequently experienced rapid economic development, but earnings from the country's oil wealth have not reached the population and the country ranks low on the UN human development index. Some 20% of children die before age 5 and more than 50% of the population lacks access to clean
       <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">
        drinking water
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo" title="Teodoro Obiang Nguema Mbasogo">
        President Teodoro Obiang
       </a>
       is widely suspected of using the country's oil wealth to enrich himself
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-global-33">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and his associates. In 2006, Forbes estimated his personal wealth at $600 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, the government announced it was planning a new capital for the country, named
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Oyala" title="Oyala">
         Oyala
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of February 2016, Obiang is Africa's longest serving dictator.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Politics of Equatorial Guinea">
        Politics of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2544" data-file-width="3392" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/280px-Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/420px-Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg/560px-Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo_with_Obamas_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Obiang and U.S. President
         <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
          Obama
         </a>
         with their wives in 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="1000" height="372" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/300px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/450px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/600px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
          Equatorial Guinea
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The current president of Equatorial Guinea is Teodoro Obiang. The 1982 constitution of Equatorial Guinea gives him extensive powers, including naming and dismissing members of the cabinet, making laws by decree, dissolving the Chamber of Representatives, negotiating and ratifying treaties and serving as commander in chief of the armed forces. Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Ehate_Tomi" title="Vicente Ehate Tomi">
        Vicente Ehate Tomi
       </a>
       was appointed by Obiang and operates under powers delegated by the President.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the three decades of his rule, Obiang has shown little tolerance for opposition. While the country is nominally a multiparty democracy, its elections have generally been considered a sham. According to
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">
        Human Rights Watch
       </a>
       , the dictatorship of President Obiang used an
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_boom" title="Oil boom">
        oil boom
       </a>
       to entrench and enrich itself further at the expense of the country's people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-40">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since August 1979 some 12 real and perceived unsuccessful coup attempts have occurred.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRW_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HRW-41">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to a March 2004 BBC profile,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       politics within the country are currently dominated by tensions between Obiang's son,
       <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Nguema_Obiang_Mangue" title="Teodoro Nguema Obiang Mangue">
        Teodoro Nguema Obiang Mangue
       </a>
       , and other close relatives with powerful positions in the security forces. The tension may be rooted in a power shift arising from the dramatic increase in oil production which has occurred since 1997.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2004 a plane load of suspected mercenaries was intercepted in
       <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
        Zimbabwe
       </a>
       while allegedly on the way to overthrow Obiang. A November 2004 report
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       named
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Thatcher" title="Mark Thatcher">
        Mark Thatcher
       </a>
       as a financial backer of the
       <a href="/wiki/2004_Equatorial_Guinea_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2004 Equatorial Guinea coup d'état attempt">
        2004 Equatorial Guinea coup d'état attempt
       </a>
       organized by
       <a href="/wiki/Simon_Mann" title="Simon Mann">
        Simon Mann
       </a>
       . Various accounts also named the United Kingdom's
       <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">
        MI6
       </a>
       , the United States'
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">
        CIA
       </a>
       , and Spain as tacit supporters of the coup attempt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nevertheless, the
       <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
        Amnesty International
       </a>
       report released in June 2005
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       on the ensuing trial of those allegedly involved highlighted the prosecution's failure to produce conclusive evidence that a coup attempt had actually taken place. Simon Mann was released from prison on 3 November 2009 for humanitarian reasons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2004
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        US Senate
       </a>
       investigation into the Washington-based
       <a href="/wiki/Riggs_Bank" title="Riggs Bank">
        Riggs Bank
       </a>
       found that President Obiang's family had received huge payments from US oil companies such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exxon_Mobil" title="Exxon Mobil">
        Exxon Mobil
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amerada_Hess" title="Amerada Hess">
        Amerada Hess
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 2005,
       <a href="/wiki/Military_Professional_Resources_Inc." title="Military Professional Resources Inc.">
        Military Professional Resources Inc.
       </a>
       , a US-based international private military company, has worked in Equatorial Guinea to train police forces in appropriate human rights practices. In 2006,
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">
        US Secretary of State
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">
        Condoleezza Rice
       </a>
       hailed Obiang as a "good friend" despite repeated criticism of his human rights and civil liberties record. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Agency_for_International_Development" title="US Agency for International Development">
        US Agency for International Development
       </a>
       entered into a memorandum of understanding (MOU) with Obiang, in April 2006, to establish a social development Fund in the country, implementing projects in the areas of health, education, women's affairs and the environment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006, Obiang signed an anti-torture decree banning all forms of abuse and improper treatment in Equatorial Guinea, and commissioned the renovation and modernization of Black Beach prison in 2007 to ensure the humane treatment of prisoners,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, human rights abuses have continued. Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International among other non-governmental organizations have documented severe human rights abuses in prisons, including torture, beatings, unexplained deaths and illegal detention.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The anti-corruption lobby
       <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">
        Transparency International
       </a>
       put Equatorial Guinea in the top 12 of its list of most corrupt states. Freedom House, a pro-democracy and human rights NGO, described Obiang as one of the world’s “most kleptocratic living autocrats,” and complained about the US government welcoming his administration and buying oil from it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dismissing international voices that call for more transparency, Obiang has long held that oil revenues are a state secret. In 2008 the country became a candidate of the
       <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">
        Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative
       </a>
       – an international project meant to promote openness about government oil revenues – but failed to qualify before an April 2010 deadline. The advocacy group
       <a href="/wiki/Global_Witness" title="Global Witness">
        Global Witness
       </a>
       has lobbying the United States to act against Obiang's son, Teodorin, vice-president and a government minister. It says there is credible evidence that he spent millions buying a
       <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">
        Malibu, California
       </a>
       mansion and private jet using corruptly acquired funds – grounds for denying him a visa.
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 2010, Equatorial Guinea signed a contract with the MPRI subsidiary of the US defense corporation
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L3_Communications" title="L3 Communications">
        L3 Communications
       </a>
       for coastal surveillance and maritime security in the Gulf of Guinea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Obiang was re-elected to serve an additional term in 2009 in an election the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        African Union
       </a>
       deemed "in line with electoral law".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Obiang re-appointed Prime Minister Ignacio Milam Tang in 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under Obiang, the basic
       <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">
        infrastructure
       </a>
       of Equatorial Guinea has improved.
       <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">
        Asphalt
       </a>
       now covers more than 80% of the national roads and ports and airports are being built by Chinese, Moroccan and French contractors across much of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-56">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, when a British parliamentary and press entourage toured the country as guests of the president in 2011,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">
         The Guardian
        </a>
       </i>
       newspaper reported that very few of Equatorial Guinea's citizens seem to benefit from improvements, with reports of empty three-lane highways and many empty buildings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Obiang regime is an ally of the USA. During a meeting on the sidelines of the recent
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
        United Nations General Assembly
       </a>
       , Obiang urged the US to strengthen cooperation between the United States and Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-56">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       President
       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
        Barack Obama
       </a>
       posed for an official photograph with President Obiang at a New York reception.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_40-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-40">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 2011, a new constitution was approved. The vote on the constitution was taken though neither the text or its content was revealed to the public before the vote. Under the new constitution the president was limited to a maximum of two seven-year terms and would be both the head of state and head of the government, therefore eliminating the prime minister. The new constitution also introduced the figure of a vice president and called for the creation of a 70-member senate with 55 senators elected by the people and the 15 remaining designated by the president. Surprisingly, in the following cabinet reshuffle it was announced that there would be two vice-presidents in clear violation of the constitution that was just taking effect.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2012, during an interview with
       <a href="/wiki/Christiane_Amanpour" title="Christiane Amanpour">
        Christiane Amanpour
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
        CNN
       </a>
       , Obiang was asked whether he would step down at the end of the current term (2009–2016) since the new constitution limited the number of terms to two and he has been reelected at least 4 times. Obiang answered he refused to step aside because the new constitution was not retroactive and the two- term limit would only become applicable from 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       26 May 2013 elections combined the senate, lower house and mayoral contests all in a single package. Like all previous elections, this was denounced by the opposition and it too was won by Obiang's PDGE. During the electoral contest, the ruling party hosted internal elections which were later scrapped as none of the president's favorite candidates led the internal lists. Ultimately, the ruling party and the satellites of the ruling coalition decided to run not based on the candidates but based on the party. This created a situation where during the election the ruling party's coalition did not provide the names of their candidates so effectively individuals were not running for office, instead the party was the one running for office.
      </p>
      <p>
       The May 2013 elections were marked by a series of events including the popular protest planned by a group of activists from the MPP (Movement of Popular Protest) which included several social and political groups. The MPP called for a peaceful protest at the Plaza de la Mujer square on 15 May. MPP coordinator Enrique Nsolo Nzo was arrested and official state media portrayed him as planning to destabilize the country and depose the president. However, and despite speaking under duress and with clear signs of torture, Nsolo said that they had planned a peaceful protest and had indeed obtained all the legal authorizations required to carry out the peaceful protest. In addition to that, he firmly stated that he was not affiliated with any political party. The Plaza de la Mujer square in Malabo was occupied by the police from 13 May and it has been heavily guarded ever since. The government embarked on a
       <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">
        censorship
       </a>
       program that affected social sites including Facebook and other websites that were critical to the government of Equatorial Guinea. The censorship was implemented by redirecting online searches to the official government website.
      </p>
      <p>
       Shortly after the elections, opposition party CPDS announced that they were going to protest peacefully against the 26 May elections on 25 June.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Interior minister Clemente Engonga refused to authorize the protest on the grounds that it could "destabilize" the country and CPDS decided to go forward, claiming constitutional right. On the night of 24 June, the CPDS headquarters in Malabo were surrounded by heavily armed police officers to keep those inside from leaving and thus effectively blocking the protest. Several leading members of CPDS were detained in Malabo and others in Bata were kept from boarding several local flights to Malabo.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Geography of Equatorial Guinea">
        Geography of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea is in west central Africa. The country consists of a mainland territory,
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">
        Río Muni
       </a>
       , which is bordered by Cameroon to the north and Gabon to the east and south, and five small islands,
       <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">
        Bioko
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Corisco" title="Corisco">
        Corisco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n" title="Annobón">
        Annobón
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Chico" title="Elobey Chico">
        Elobey Chico
       </a>
       (Small Elobey), and
       <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Grande" title="Elobey Grande">
        Elobey Grande
       </a>
       (Great Elobey). Bioko, the site of the capital, Malabo, lies about 40 kilometers (25 mi) off the coast of Cameroon. Annobón Island is about 350 kilometers (220 mi) west-south-west of
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lopez" title="Cape Lopez">
        Cape Lopez
       </a>
       in Gabon. Corisco and the two Elobey islands are in Corisco Bay, on the border of Río Muni and Gabon.
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_north" title="4th parallel north">
        4°N
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_south" title="2nd parallel south">
        2°S
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/5th_meridian_west" title="5th meridian west">
        5°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">
        12°E
       </a>
       . Despite its name, no part of the country's territory lies on the equator—it is in the northern hemisphere, except for the insular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" title="Annobón Province">
        Annobón Province
       </a>
       , which is about 155 km (96 mi) south of the equator.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea has a tropical climate with distinct wet and dry seasons. From June to August, Río Muni is dry and Bioko wet; from December to February, the reverse occurs. In between there is gradual transition. Rain or mist occurs daily on Annobón, where a cloudless day has never been registered. The temperature at Malabo, Bioko, ranges from 16 °C (61 °F) to 33 °C (91 °F), though on the southern
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Moka_Plateau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Moka Plateau (page does not exist)">
        Moka Plateau
       </a>
       normal high temperatures are only 21 °C (70 °F). In Río Muni, the average temperature is about 27 °C (81 °F). Annual
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainfall" title="Rainfall">
        rainfall
       </a>
       varied from 1,930 mm (76 in) at Malabo to 10,920 mm (430 in) at
       <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_de_Ureca" title="San Antonio de Ureca">
        Ureka
       </a>
       , Bioko, but Río Muni is somewhat drier.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea spans several
       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
        ecoregions
       </a>
       . Río Muni region lies within the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Equatorial_coastal_forests" title="Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests">
        Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests
       </a>
       ecoregion except for patches of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_African_mangroves" title="Central African mangroves">
        Central African mangroves
       </a>
       on the coast, especially in the
       <a href="/wiki/Muni_River" title="Muni River">
        Muni River
       </a>
       estuary. The
       <a href="/wiki/Cross-Sanaga-Bioko_coastal_forests" title="Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests">
        Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests
       </a>
       ecoregion covers most of Bioko and the adjacent portions of
       <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">
        Cameroon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       on the African mainland, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon_and_Bioko_montane_forests" title="Mount Cameroon and Bioko montane forests">
        Mount Cameroon and Bioko montane forests
       </a>
       ecoregion covers the highlands of Bioko and nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">
        Mount Cameroon
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9,_Pr%C3%ADncipe,_and_Annob%C3%B3n_moist_lowland_forests" title="São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests">
        São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests
       </a>
       ecoregion covers all of Annobón, as well as São Tomé and Príncipe.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Provinces of Equatorial Guinea">
        Provinces of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 205px; width: 350px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_1_1796402777">
         <area alt="Annobón Province" coords="12,128,38,171" href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" shape="rect" title="Annobón Province"/>
         <area alt="Bioko Norte Province" coords="37,7,68,41" href="/wiki/Bioko_Norte_Province" shape="rect" title="Bioko Norte Province"/>
         <area alt="Bioko Sur Province" coords="19,48,50,83" href="/wiki/Bioko_Sur_Province" shape="rect" title="Bioko Sur Province"/>
         <area alt="Centro Sur Province" coords="184,90,219,129" href="/wiki/Centro_Sur_Province" shape="rect" title="Centro Sur Province"/>
         <area alt="Kié-Ntem Province" coords="296,29,328,68" href="/wiki/Ki%C3%A9-Ntem_Province" shape="rect" title="Kié-Ntem Province"/>
         <area alt="Litoral Province (Equatorial Guinea)" coords="106,89,138,129" href="/wiki/Litoral_Province_(Equatorial_Guinea)" shape="rect" title="Litoral Province (Equatorial Guinea)"/>
         <area alt="Wele-Nzas Province" coords="283,111,318,154" href="/wiki/Wele-Nzas_Province" shape="rect" title="Wele-Nzas Province"/>
        </map>
        <img alt="A clickable map of Equatorial Guinea exhibiting its two regions and seven provinces." data-file-height="176" data-file-width="300" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Equatorial_Guinea_provinces_numbered.png" usemap="#ImageMap_1_1796402777" width="350"/>
        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea_provinces_numbered.png" title="About this image">
          <img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea is divided into eight provinces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statoids_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-statoids-62">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The newest province is
       <a href="/wiki/Djibloho" title="Djibloho">
        Djibloho
       </a>
       , created in 2017 with its headquarters at
       <a href="/wiki/Oyala" title="Oyala">
        Oyala
       </a>
       , the country's future capital.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The other seven provinces are as follows (capitals appear in parentheses):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statoids_62-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-statoids-62">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n" title="Annobón">
         Annobón
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_de_Pal%C3%A9" title="San Antonio de Palé">
         San Antonio de Palé
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bioko_Norte" title="Bioko Norte">
         Bioko Norte
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">
         Malabo
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bioko_Sur" title="Bioko Sur">
         Bioko Sur
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Luba,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Luba, Equatorial Guinea">
         Luba
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Centro_Sur" title="Centro Sur">
         Centro Sur
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Evinayong" title="Evinayong">
         Evinayong
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ki%C3%A9-Ntem" title="Kié-Ntem">
         Kié-Ntem
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Ebebiy%C3%ADn" title="Ebebiyín">
         Ebebiyín
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Litoral_(Equatorial_Guinea)" title="Litoral (Equatorial Guinea)">
         Litoral
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">
         Bata
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Wele-Nzas" title="Wele-Nzas">
         Wele-Nzas
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Mongomo" title="Mongomo">
         Mongomo
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The provinces are further divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Municipalities of Equatorial Guinea">
        districts
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Economy of Equatorial Guinea">
        Economy of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="861" data-file-width="1104" height="351" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg/450px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg/675px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg/900px-Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg 2x" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_exports_2009_Equatorial_Guinea.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A proportional representation of Equatorial Guinea's exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Before independence Equatorial Guinea exported
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       , coffee and timber, mostly to its colonial ruler, Spain, but also to Germany and the UK. On 1 January 1985, the country became the first non-
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Francophone" title="wikt:Francophone">
        Francophone
       </a>
       African member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franc_zone" title="Franc zone">
        franc zone
       </a>
       , adopting the
       <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">
        CFA franc
       </a>
       as its currency. The national currency, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ekwele" title="Ekwele">
        ekwele
       </a>
       , has previously been linked to the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">
        Spanish peseta
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-67">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The discovery of large
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">
        oil reserves
       </a>
       in 1996 and its subsequent exploitation contributed to a dramatic increase in government revenue. As of 2004
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Equatorial Guinea is the third-largest oil producer in
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        Sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       . Its oil production has risen to 360,000 barrels per day (57,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       /d), up from 220,000 only two years earlier.
      </p>
      <p>
       Forestry, farming, and fishing are also major components of GDP. Subsistence farming predominates. The deterioration of the rural economy under successive brutal regimes has diminished any potential for agriculture-led growth.
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2004, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">
        United States Senate
       </a>
       published an investigation into
       <a href="/wiki/Riggs_Bank" title="Riggs Bank">
        Riggs Bank
       </a>
       , a Washington-based bank into which most of Equatorial Guinea's oil revenues were paid until recently, and which also banked for
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">
        Augusto Pinochet
       </a>
       . The Senate report showed at least $35 million siphoned off by Obiang, his family and regime senior officials. The president has denied any wrongdoing. Riggs Bank in February 2005 paid $9 million in restitution for Pinochet's banking, no restitution was made with regard to Equatorial Guinea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 2000 to 2010, Equatorial Guinea had the highest average annual increase in GDP (Gross Domestic Product), 17%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea is a member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">
        Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">
        OHADA
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohada.com_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-71">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Equatorial Guinea tried to be validated as an
       <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">
        Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative
       </a>
       (EITI)–compliant country, working toward transparency in reporting of oil revenues and prudent use of natural resource wealth. The country obtained candidate status on 22 February 2008. It was then required to meet a number of obligations to do so, including committing to working with civil society and companies on EITI implementation, appointing a senior individual to lead on EITI implementation, and publishing a fully costed Work Plan with measurable targets, a timetable for implementation and an assessment of capacity constraints. However, when Equatorial Guinea applied to extend the deadline for completing EITI validation, the EITI Board did not agree to the extension.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       , Equatorial Guinea has the highest GNI (Gross National Income) per capita of any sub-Saharan country, 83 times larger than the GNI per capita of
       <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">
        Burundi
       </a>
       , the poorest country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Transport in Equatorial Guinea">
        Transport in Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Due to the large oil industry in the country, internationally recognized carriers fly to
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">
        Malabo International Airport
       </a>
       which, in May 2014, had several direct connections to
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
        West Africa
       </a>
       . There are three airports in Equatorial Guinea —
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">
        Malabo International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bata_Airport" title="Bata Airport">
        Bata Airport
       </a>
       and the new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annobon_Airport" title="Annobon Airport">
        Annobon Airport
       </a>
       on the island of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annobon" title="Annobon">
        Annobon
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">
        Malabo International Airport
       </a>
       is the only international airport
      </p>
      <p>
       Every airline registered in Equatorial Guinea appears on the list of air carriers prohibited in the
