       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       (EU) which means that they are banned from operating services of any kind within the EU.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However freight carriers provide service from European cities to the capital.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Demographics of Equatorial Guinea">
        Demographics of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bubi_children.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="143" data-file-width="227" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Bubi_children.jpg/220px-Bubi_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fa/Bubi_children.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bubi_children.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Equatorial Guinean children of
         <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
          Bubi
         </a>
         descent.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The majority of the people of Equatorial Guinea are of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_people" title="Bantu people">
        Bantu
       </a>
       origin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The largest ethnic group, the
       <a href="/wiki/Fang_people" title="Fang people">
        Fang
       </a>
       , is indigenous to the mainland, but substantial migration to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioko_Island" title="Bioko Island">
        Bioko Island
       </a>
       since the 20th century means the Fang population exceeds that of the earlier
       <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
        Bubi
       </a>
       inhabitants. The Fang constitute 80% of the population
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and comprise around 67 clans. Those in the northern part of
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">
        Río Muni
       </a>
       speak Fang-Ntumu, while those in the south speak Fang-Okah; the two dialects have differences but are mutually intelligible. Dialects of Fang are also spoken in parts of neighboring Cameroon (Bulu) and Gabon. These dialects, while still intelligible, are more distinct. The
       <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">
        Bubi
       </a>
       , who constitute 15% of the population, are indigenous to Bioko Island. The traditional demarcation line between Fang and 'Beach' (inland) ethnic groups was the village of
       <a href="/wiki/Niefang" title="Niefang">
        Niefang
       </a>
       (limit of the Fang), east of Bata.
      </p>
      <p>
       Coastal ethnic groups, sometimes referred to as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ndowe" title="Ndowe">
        Ndowe
       </a>
       or "Playeros" (
       <i>
        Beach People
       </i>
       in Spanish):
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combe_people" title="Combe people">
        Combes
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bujeba_people" title="Bujeba people">
        Bujebas
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balengue_people" title="Balengue people">
        Balengues
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Benga_people" title="Benga people">
        Bengas
       </a>
       on the mainland and small islands, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fernandinos" title="Fernandinos">
        Fernandinos
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Krio_people" title="Sierra Leone Krio people">
        Krio
       </a>
       community on Bioko Island. together comprise 5% of the population. Europeans (largely of Spanish or
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       descent, some with partial African ancestry) also live in the country, but most ethnic Spaniards left after independence.
      </p>
      <p>
       A growing number of foreigners from neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">
        Cameroon
       </a>
       , Nigeria, and
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       have immigrated to the country. According to the
       <i>
        Encyclopedia of the Stateless Nations
       </i>
       (2002) 7% of Bioko islanders were
       <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">
        Igbo
       </a>
       , an ethnic group from southeastern Nigeria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Equatorial Guinea received
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asians" title="Asians">
        Asians
       </a>
       and black Africans from other countries as workers on cocoa and coffee plantations. Other black Africans came from
       <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">
        Liberia
       </a>
       , Angola, and
       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">
        Mozambique
       </a>
       . Most of the Asian population is
       <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">
        Chinese
       </a>
       , with small numbers of
       <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">
        Indians
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea has also been a destination for fortune-seeking European settlers from Britain, France and Germany. Israelis and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" title="Moroccan people">
        Moroccans
       </a>
       also live and work here.
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        Oil extraction
       </a>
       since the 1990s has contributed to a doubling of the population in Malabo. After independence, thousands of Equatorial Guineans went to Spain. Another 100,000 Equatorial Guineans went to Cameroon, Gabon, and Nigeria because of the dictatorship of
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mac%C3%ADas_Nguema" title="Francisco Macías Nguema">
        Francisco Macías Nguema
       </a>
       . Some Equatorial Guinean communities are also found in Latin America, the United States, Portugal, and France.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       For years, the official languages were
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       (the local variant is
       <a href="/wiki/Equatoguinean_Spanish" title="Equatoguinean Spanish">
        Equatoguinean Spanish
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Portuguese was also adopted as an official language later in 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP-78">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sol_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sol-79">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish has been an official language since 1844. It is still the language of education and administration. 67.6% of Equatorial Guineans can speak it, especially those living in the capital,
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">
        Malabo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obi_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-obi-80">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French was only made official in order to join the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Francophonie
       </a>
       and it is not locally spoken, except in some border towns.
      </p>
      <p>
       Aboriginal languages are recognized as integral parts of the "national culture" (Constitutional Law No. 1/1998 January 21). Indigenous languages include
       <a href="/wiki/Fang_language" title="Fang language">
        Fang
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bube_language" title="Bube language">
        Bube
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Benga_language" title="Benga language">
        Benga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combe_language" title="Combe language">
        Ndowe
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balengue_language" title="Balengue language">
        Balengue
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bujeba_language" title="Bujeba language">
        Bujeba
       </a>
       , Bissio, Gumu, Igbo,
       <a href="/wiki/Pichinglis" title="Pichinglis">
        Pichinglis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annobonese_language" title="Annobonese language">
        Fa d’Ambô
       </a>
       and the nearly extinct
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseke_language" title="Baseke language">
        Baseke
       </a>
       . Most African ethnic groups speak
       <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">
        Bantu languages
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GEpress_noticia134en_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GEpress_noticia134en-81">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annobonese_language" title="Annobonese language">
        Fa d’Ambô
       </a>
       , a Portuguese creole, has vigorous use in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" title="Annobón Province">
        Annobón Province
       </a>
       , in Malabo (the capital), and among some speakers in Equatorial Guinea's mainland. Many residents of Bioko can also speak Spanish, particularly in the capital, and the local trade language
       <a href="/wiki/Pichinglis" title="Pichinglis">
        Pichinglis
       </a>
       , an English-based creole. Spanish is not spoken much in Annobón. In government and education Spanish is used. Noncreolized Portuguese is used as liturgical language by local Catholics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Annobonese ethnic community tried to gain membership in the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">
        Community of Portuguese Language Countries
       </a>
       (CPLP). The government financed an
       <a href="/wiki/International_Portuguese_Language_Institute" title="International Portuguese Language Institute">
        Instituto Internacional da Língua Portuguesa
       </a>
       (IILP) sociolinguistic study in Annobón. It documented strong links with the Portuguese creole populations in São Tomé and Príncipe, Cape Verde and Guinea-Bissau.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sol_79-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sol-79">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to historical and cultural ties, in 2010 the legislature amended article four of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Constitution of Equatorial Guinea">
        Constitution of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
       , to establish Portuguese as an official language of the Republic. This was an effort by the government to improve its communications, trade, and bilateral relations with Portuguese-speaking countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuineEqGov_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GuineEqGov-84">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuineEqGovPDF_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GuineEqGovPDF-85">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It also recognizes long historical ties with Portugal, and with Portuguese-speaking peoples of Brazil, São Tomé and Principe, and Cape Verde.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the motivations for Equatorial Guinea's membership pursuit into the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">
        Community of Portuguese Language Countries
       </a>
       (CPLP) included access to several professional and academic exchange programs and facilitated cross-border circulation of citizens.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obi_80-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-obi-80">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The adoption of Portuguese as an official language was the primary requirement to apply for CPLP acceptance. In addition, the country was told it must adopt political reforms allowing effective democracy and respect for human rights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The national parliament discussed this law in October 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GEpress_noticia1980_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GEpress_noticia1980-87">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 2012, Equatorial Guinea's foreign minister signed an agreement with the IILP on the promotion of Portuguese in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IILP_Blog2012-02-07_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IILP_Blog2012-02-07-88">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_News1875_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP_News1875-89">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2012, the CPLP refused Equatorial Guinea full membership, primarily because of its continued serious violations of human rights. The government responded by legalizing political parties, declaring a moratorium on the death penalty, and starting a dialog with all political factions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sol_79-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-sol-79">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expr_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-expr-90">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, the IILP secured land from the government for the construction of Portuguese language cultural centres in Bata and Malabo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sol_79-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-sol-79">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At its 10th summit in
       <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">
        Dili
       </a>
       in July 2014, Equatorial Guinea was admitted as a CPLP member. Abolition of the death penalty and the promotion of Portuguese as an official language were preconditions of the approval.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_NewsID1635_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP_NewsID1635-91">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:#ddd">
          <th colspan="5">
           Religion in Equatorial Guinea
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
          <td style="padding:0 4px;">
           Religion
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
          </td>
          <td style="width:100px;">
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">
           percent
          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Roman Catholicism in Equatorial Guinea">
            Roman Catholic
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:Blue; width:87%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           87%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Other (indigenous beliefs /
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i" title="Baha'i">
            Baha'i
           </a>
           )
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:Gray; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           5%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
            Protestant
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:green; width:5%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           5%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">
            Islam
           </a>
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:Green; width:2%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           2%
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The principal religion in Equatorial Guinea is Christianity, the faith of 93% of the population.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Roman Catholicism in Equatorial Guinea">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       make up the majority (87%), while a minority are Protestants (5%). 2% of the population follows
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">
        Islam
       </a>
       (mainly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">
        Sunni
       </a>
       ). The remaining 5% practise
       <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">
        Animism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bahá'í Faith in Equatorial Guinea">
        Bahá'í Faith
       </a>
       , and other beliefs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Health">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Health in Equatorial Guinea">
        Health in Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea’s innovative
       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">
        malaria
       </a>
       programs in the early 21st century achieved success in reducing
       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">
        malaria
       </a>
       infection, disease, and
       <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">
        mortality
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Their program consists of twice-yearly indoor residual spraying (IRS), the introduction of artemisinin combination treatment (ACTs), the use of intermittent preventive treatment in pregnant women (IPTp), and the introduction of very high coverage with long-lasting insecticide-treated mosquito nets (LLINs). Their efforts resulted in a reduction in all-cause under-five mortality from 152 to 55 deaths per 1,000 live births (down 64%), a sharp drop that coincided with the launch of the program.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2014 four cases of
       <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">
        polio
       </a>
       were reported, the country's first outbreak of the disease.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EquatorialGuinea_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EquatorialGuinea-95">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Education in Equatorial Guinea">
        Education in Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Macias" title="Francisco Macias">
        Francisco Macias
       </a>
       , education was neglected, and few children received any type of education. Under President Obiang, the illiteracy rate dropped from 73% to 13%,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_6-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the number of primary school students rose from 65,000 in 1986 to more than 100,000 in 1994. Education is free and compulsory for children between the ages of 6 and 14.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_67-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-67">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Equatorial Guinea government has partnered with
       <a href="/wiki/Hess_Corporation" title="Hess Corporation">
        Hess Corporation
       </a>
       and The Academy for Educational Development (AED) to establish a $20 million education program for primary school teachers to teach modern child development techniques.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are now 51 model schools whose active pedagogy will be a national reform.
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years, with change in economic/political climate and government social agendas, several cultural dispersion and literacy organizations have been founded, chiefly with the financial support of the Spanish government. The country has one university, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Nacional_de_Guinea_Ecuatorial" title="Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial">
        Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial
       </a>
       (UNGE), with a campus in Malabo and a Faculty of Medicine located in Bata on the mainland. In 2009 the university produced the first 110 national doctors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_56-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-56">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Bata Medical School is supported principally by the government of Cuba and staffed by Cuban medical educators and physicians. Equatorial Guinea predicts that it will have enough national doctors in the country to be self-sufficient within the next five years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_56-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-56">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Culture of Equatorial Guinea">
        Culture of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1792" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/300px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/450px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/600px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The port of
         <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">
          Malabo
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In June 1984, the First Hispanic-African Cultural Congress was convened to explore the cultural identity of Equatorial Guinea. The congress constituted the center of integration and the marriage of the Hispanic culture with African cultures.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_67-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-67">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea currently has no
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">
        UNESCO World Heritage Site
       </a>
       or tentative sites for the World Heritage List.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country also has no documented heritage listed in the
       <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme" title="Memory of the World Programme">
        Memory of the World Programme
       </a>
       of UNESCO nor any intangible cultural heritage listed in the UNESCO
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intangible_Cultural_Heritage" title="Intangible Cultural Heritage">
        Intangible Cultural Heritage
       </a>
       List.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">
        Media and communications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media and communications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Media in Equatorial Guinea">
        Media in Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea">
        Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The principal means of communication within Equatorial Guinea are three state-operated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio">
        FM radio
       </a>
       stations.
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">
        BBC World Service
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_France_Internationale" title="Radio France Internationale">
        Radio France Internationale
       </a>
       and Gabon-based Africa No 1 broadcast on FM in Malabo. There are also five
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shortwave" title="Shortwave">
        shortwave
       </a>
       radio stations. Television Nacional, the television network, is state operated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_6-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The international TV programme RTVGE is available via satellites in Africa, Europa, and the Americas and worldwide via Internet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyngsat_TVGE_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lyngsat_TVGE-101">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are two newspapers and two magazines.
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea ranks at position 161 out of 179 countries in the 2012
       <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
        Reporters Without Borders
       </a>
       press freedom index. The watchdog says the national broadcaster obeys the orders of the information ministry. A "news blackout" was imposed on reporting of uprisings in Arab states in North Africa in 2011, according to the Committee to Protect Journalists. Most of the media companies practice heavy
       <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">
        self-censorship
       </a>
       , and are banned by law from criticising public figures. The state-owned media and the main private radio station are under the directorship of the president's son, Teodor Obiang.
      </p>
      <p>
       Landline telephone penetration is low, with only two lines available for every 100 persons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_6-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is one
       <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">
        GSM
       </a>
       mobile telephone operator, with coverage of
       <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">
        Malabo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">
        Bata
       </a>
       , and several mainland cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2009
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , approximately 40% of the population subscribed to mobile telephone services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_6-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The only telephone provider in Equatorial Guinea is Orange.
      </p>
      <p>
       There were more than 42,000 internet users by December 2011.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Music of Equatorial Guinea">
        Music of Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       There is little
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">
        popular music
       </a>
       coming out of Equatorial Guinea. Pan-African styles like
       <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">
        soukous
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">
        makossa
       </a>
       are popular, as are
       <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">
        reggae
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">
        rock and roll
       </a>
       . Acoustic guitar bands based on a Spanish model are the country's best-known indigenous popular tradition.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_at_the_Olympics" title="Equatorial Guinea at the Olympics">
        Equatorial Guinea at the Olympics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea national football team">
        Equatorial Guinea national football team
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea women's national football team">
        Equatorial Guinea women's national football team
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_national_basketball_team" title="Equatorial Guinea national basketball team">
        Equatorial Guinea national basketball team
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea was chosen to co-host the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 African Cup of Nations">
        2012 African Cup of Nations
       </a>
       in partnership with
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       , and hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">
        2015 edition
       </a>
       . The country was also chosen to host the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Women%27s_African_Football_Championship" title="2008 Women's African Football Championship">
        2008 Women's African Football Championship
       </a>
       , which they won. The
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea women's national football team">
        women's national team
       </a>
       qualified for the
       <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">
        2011 World Cup
       </a>
       in Germany.
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2016, Equatorial Guinea was chosen to host the
       <a href="/wiki/2019_African_Games" title="2019 African Games">
        12th African Games
       </a>
       in 2019.
      </p>
      <p>
       Equatorial Guinea is famous for the swimmers
       <a href="/wiki/Eric_Moussambani" title="Eric Moussambani">
        Eric Moussambani
       </a>
       , nicknamed "Eric the Eel",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Paula_Barila_Bolopa" title="Paula Barila Bolopa">
        Paula Barila Bolopa
       </a>
       , "Paula the Crawler", who had astoundingly slow times at the
       <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">
        2000 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-1">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-1">
             ^
